# NBA Visual Materials

**Degree Path:** Doctor of Professional Basketball Officiating - NBA Elite Concentration
**Academic Level:** Doctoral Professional Residency
**Course Cover:** `frontend/public/assets/images/refzone/course-covers/nba.svg`

## Course Overview

This track is designed for elite professional basketball officials preparing for NBA-style rule administration, Replay Center interaction, Coach’s Challenge procedures, professional crew hierarchy, and national-level performance analytics. Students in this track study the full annual officiating cycle through classroom lecture, court mechanics, film laboratory, role-play, live practicum, mentoring, written exams, oral defense, and advancement board review. The teaching emphasis throughout the year is to develop officials who think, prepare, communicate, and self-scout like elite professional basketball officials.

## Course Image Brief

**Visual Elements:** elite professional basketball arena with national broadcast lights, Replay Center monitor wall, coach challenge signal card, professional crew hierarchy board, analytics dashboard, whistle, and polished hardwood
**Visual Emphasis:** NBA-style rule administration, replay interaction, coach challenge procedures, analytics, and elite professional preparation
**Image Prompt:** Create a RefZone University course-card image for NBA: elite professional basketball arena with national broadcast lights, Replay Center monitor wall, coach challenge signal card, professional crew hierarchy board, analytics dashboard, whistle, and polished hardwood. Emphasize NBA-style rule administration, replay interaction, coach challenge procedures, analytics, and elite professional preparation. Use a premium basketball officiating education style with black, metallic silver, white, and orange accents, clean readable course title text, dramatic court lighting, and professional academic training energy. Avoid real school logos, real league logos, and recognizable real people.

## Graduation Requirements

- Complete all 52 weeks of daily academic work.
- Pass all written rules and philosophy examinations.
- Complete every film-lab assignment and full-game self-scout.
- Demonstrate mechanics competence in two-person and three-person systems appropriate to the track.
- Complete role-play scenarios involving coaches, players, partners, table crew, observers, and supervisors.
- Submit required reports for technical, flagrant, administrative, spectator, facility, and unusual situations applicable to the track.
- Complete live-practicum observations and receive mentor/evaluator approval.
- Defend final portfolio before the RTBO advancement board.

## Weekly Materials

### Week 1: Orientation and Professional Identity

- Screenshot package: learner screen, week overview, active lesson view, and progress state.
- Presentation source: `docs/refzone-university/presentation-outlines/nba-presentation.md#week-1`.
- Required evidence: Students must produce a written journal entry, a film-lab worksheet, a court-lab rubric, a role-play score, and a mentor note showing how Orientation and Professional Identity affects the NBA environment. If a student cannot produce evidence, the week is not complete.
- Day 1: Professor Lecture and Socratic Seminar - Professor Lecture; visual `/assets/images/refzone/lesson-visuals/lecture.svg`.
  - Screenshot: `/assets/images/refzone/course-screenshots/nba-lecture.svg`.
  - Required reading: Read the current NBA official rules and officiating points of emphasis sections tied to NBA basketball officiating professionalism, rule readiness, crew communication, game administration, and player safety; mark definitions, penalties, exceptions, and restart language that control live-game rulings. Read the NBA game reports, replay examples, and approved training clips connected to NBA basketball officiating professionalism, rule readiness, crew communication, game administration, and player safety; write the ruling, the reason, the crew responsibility, and the best supervisor explanation. Study the professional mechanics, coverage, replay, and communication directives for the day's NBA basketball officiating professionalism, rule readiness, crew communication, game administration, and player safety coverage problem; draw the official's starting position, movement path, primary area, secondary awareness, and reporting route. Review league professionalism, bench control, altercation, and public-pressure standards; identify the correct professional response when a coach, player, partner, table crew, observer, or supervisor challenges the ruling. Study the professor lecture visual aid and screenshot packet; bring one film, court, or written example that proves how NBA basketball officiating professionalism, rule readiness, crew communication, game administration, and player safety changes game behavior.
  - Assignment: Submit the daily journal entry, worksheet or lab artifact, and one mentor-ready evidence item tied to NBA basketball officiating professionalism, rule readiness, crew communication, game administration, and player safety.
  - Assessment: Written Knowledge Check - 85% or mentor approval is required before Day 2 unlocks.
  - Test: NBA Week 1, Day 1 Basketball Officiating Written Knowledge Check; passing score 85%.
  - Line Item 1 - Professor Explanation: instruction-slide; Professor-facing lecture slide, visual aid, and discussion prompt.
  - Line Item 2 - What the Student Performs: student-activity; Student-facing worksheet, lab action, and participation artifact.
  - Line Item 3 - Expected Outcome, Evidence, and Grading: assessment-evidence; Assessment-facing quiz/test item, rubric row, and evidence checkpoint.

  - Required reading: Read the current NBA official rules and officiating points of emphasis sections tied to Mechanics as Visual Science in NBA basketball officiating; mark definitions, penalties, exceptions, and restart language that control live-game rulings. Read the NBA game reports, replay examples, and approved training clips connected to Mechanics as Visual Science in NBA basketball officiating; write the ruling, the reason, the crew responsibility, and the best supervisor explanation. Study the professional mechanics, coverage, replay, and communication directives for the day's Mechanics as Visual Science in NBA basketball officiating coverage problem; draw the official's starting position, movement path, primary area, secondary awareness, and reporting route. Review league professionalism, bench control, altercation, and public-pressure standards; identify the correct professional response when a coach, player, partner, table crew, observer, or supervisor challenges the ruling. Study the professor lecture visual aid and screenshot packet; bring one film, court, or written example that proves how Mechanics as Visual Science in NBA basketball officiating changes game behavior.
  - Assignment: Submit the daily journal entry, worksheet or lab artifact, and one mentor-ready evidence item tied to Mechanics as Visual Science in NBA basketball officiating.
  - Assessment: Written Knowledge Check - 85% or mentor approval is required before Day 2 unlocks.
  - Test: NBA Week 3, Day 1 Basketball Officiating Written Knowledge Check; passing score 85%.

### Week 4: Communication Psychology

- Screenshot package: learner screen, week overview, active lesson view, and progress state.
- Presentation source: `docs/refzone-university/presentation-outlines/nba-presentation.md#week-4`.
- Required evidence: Students must produce a written journal entry, a film-lab worksheet, a court-lab rubric, a role-play score, and a mentor note showing how Communication Psychology affects the NBA environment. If a student cannot produce evidence, the week is not complete.

- Presentation source: `docs/refzone-university/presentation-outlines/nba-presentation.md#week-12`.
- Required evidence: Students must produce a written journal entry, a film-lab worksheet, a court-lab rubric, a role-play score, and a mentor note showing how Free Throws, Throw-Ins, and Special Situations affects the NBA environment. If a student cannot produce evidence, the week is not complete.
- Day 1: Professor Lecture and Socratic Seminar - Professor Lecture; visual `/assets/images/refzone/lesson-visuals/lecture.svg`.
  - Screenshot: `/assets/images/refzone/course-screenshots/nba-lecture.svg`.
  - Required reading: Read the current NBA official rules and officiating points of emphasis sections tied to Free Throws, Throw-Ins, and Special Situations in NBA basketball officiating; mark definitions, penalties, exceptions, and restart language that control live-game rulings. Read the NBA game reports, replay examples, and approved training clips connected to Free Throws, Throw-Ins, and Special Situations in NBA basketball officiating; write the ruling, the reason, the crew responsibility, and the best supervisor explanation. Study the professional mechanics, coverage, replay, and communication directives for the day's Free Throws, Throw-Ins, and Special Situations in NBA basketball officiating coverage problem; draw the official's starting position, movement path, primary area, secondary awareness, and reporting route. Review league professionalism, bench control, altercation, and public-pressure standards; identify the correct professional response when a coach, player, partner, table crew, observer, or supervisor challenges the ruling. Study the professor lecture visual aid and screenshot packet; bring one film, court, or written example that proves how Free Throws, Throw-Ins, and Special Situations in NBA basketball officiating changes game behavior.
  - Assignment: Submit the daily journal entry, worksheet or lab artifact, and one mentor-ready evidence item tied to Free Throws, Throw-Ins, and Special Situations in NBA basketball officiating.
  - Assessment: Written Knowledge Check - 85% or mentor approval is required before Day 2 unlocks.
  - Test: NBA Week 12, Day 1 Basketball Officiating Written Knowledge Check; passing score 85%.
  - Line Item 1 - Professor Explanation: instruction-slide; Professor-facing lecture slide, visual aid, and discussion prompt.
  - Line Item 2 - What the Student Performs: student-activity; Student-facing worksheet, lab action, and participation artifact.
  - Line Item 3 - Expected Outcome, Evidence, and Grading: assessment-evidence; Assessment-facing quiz/test item, rubric row, and evidence checkpoint.

Review league professionalism, bench control, altercation, and public-pressure standards; identify the correct professional response when a coach, player, partner, table crew, observer, or supervisor challenges the ruling.   - Assignment: Submit the daily journal entry, worksheet or lab artifact, and one mentor-ready evidence item tied to Level-Specific Reporting Intensive as applied to NBA basketball officiating.

Review league professionalism, bench control, altercation, and public-pressure standards; identify the correct professional response when a coach, player, partner, table crew, observer, or supervisor challenges the ruling. Study the professor lecture visual aid and screenshot packet; bring one film, court, or written example that proves how Elite Preparation and Professional Habits as applied to NBA basketball officiating changes game behavior.
